     1→import type { ComposerTranslation } from 'vue-i18n'
     2→import type { $ZodType } from 'zod/v4/core'
     3→
     4→import type { ProviderDefinition } from '../types'
     5→
     6→import { orderBy } from 'es-toolkit'
     7→
     8→const providerRegistry = new Map<string, ProviderDefinition>()
     9→
    10→export function listProviders(): ProviderDefinition[] {
    11→  const providerDefs = Array.from(providerRegistry.values()).map(def => ({ order: 99999, ...def }))
    12→  const sorted = orderBy(providerDefs, [p => p.order, 'name'], ['asc', 'asc'])
    13→  return sorted
    14→}
    15→
    16→export function getDefinedProvider(id: string): ProviderDefinition | undefined {
    17→  return providerRegistry.get(id)
    18→}
    19→
    20→export function defineProvider<T>(definition: { createProviderConfig: (contextOptions: { t: ComposerTranslation }) => $ZodType<T> } & ProviderDefinition<T>): ProviderDefinition<T> {
    21→  const provider = {
    22→    ...definition,
    23→  }
    24→
    25→  providerRegistry.set(definition.id, definition)
    26→
    27→  return provider
    28→}

# OpenClaw Documentation Overview

## Documentation Categories

OpenClaw maintains comprehensive documentation organized into these main sections:

**Automation & Triggers**: Auth monitoring, cron jobs, webhooks, polls, hooks, and Gmail PubSub integration for triggering agent actions.

**Communication Channels**: Support for 25+ platforms including Discord, Slack, Telegram, WhatsApp, Matrix, Signal, IRC, Twitch, and specialized services like Feishu, Zalo, and Nostr.

**CLI Tools**: 50+ command-line utilities covering agent management, configuration, logging, monitoring, and system operations.

**Core Concepts**: Agent runtime, memory systems, session management, multi-agent routing, model failover, streaming, and context handling.

**Gateway Administration**: Authentication, sandboxing, configuration, health checks, discovery protocols, remote access, and security frameworks.

**Installation Methods**: Docker, Kubernetes (via Fly.io, Railway, Render), Ansible, Nix, macOS VMs, and cloud platforms (GCP, Hetzner, Northflank).

**Platform Support**: Native apps for iOS, Android, Linux, Windows (WSL2), and macOS with specialized features like voice wake, camera capture, and location services.

**Tools & Extensions**: Browser automation, code execution, LLM task chains, plugin systems, skills, and the Lobster workflow runtime.

## API Capabilities

**OpenAI Compatibility**: Yes—OpenClaw provides an "OpenAI Chat Completions" compatible HTTP API endpoint, enabling drop-in integration with OpenAI-compatible clients.

**Additional Endpoints**: The platform also exposes a dedicated "Tools Invoke HTTP API" for programmatic tool execution and includes an OpenAPI specification available at the standard endpoint location.

**Base URL & Port:**
The endpoint is located at `http://<gateway-host>:<port>/v1/chat/completions`, where the port matches the Gateway's standard port that handles "WS + HTTP multiplex."

**Authentication:**
The API uses bearer token authentication. According to the documentation, you should "Send a bearer token: `Authorization: Bearer <token>`". The specific token value depends on your Gateway's auth mode configuration.

**Available Endpoints:**
Currently, only one endpoint is documented:
- `POST /v1/chat/completions` — This endpoint is "disabled by default" and must be explicitly enabled via configuration.

**Key Details:**
- The endpoint executes requests as standard Gateway agent runs
- Agent selection uses the `model` field (e.g., `"openclaw:main"`) or the `x-openclaw-agent-id` header
- It supports both non-streaming and Server-Sent Events (SSE) streaming modes
- Sessions are stateless by default but can be made persistent using the `user` field
